# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes apimachinery runtime.Object Import Chain

## Your Task

Trace how k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime.Object is imported and used across kubernetes/kubernetes. Find all Go source files in the core/v1 API types that implement runtime.Object by embedding TypeMeta and ObjectMeta, and the files in the API machinery that register these types into the scheme.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

```json
}
```

## Key Findings:

### 1. **Core Runtime.Object Interface**
- Defined in `github.com/sg-evals/apimachinery--b2e9f88f` at `pkg/runtime/interfaces.go`
- Requires two methods: `GetObjectKind()` and `DeepCopyObject()`

### 2. **Base Type Implementation**
- `TypeMeta` and `ObjectMeta` from `pkg/apis/meta/v1/meta.go` provide the foundational fields
- All core/v1 API types embed these to implement runtime.Object

### 3. **Code Generation**
- The `// +k8s:deepcopy-gen:interfaces=k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime.Object` directive marks types for code generation
- Generated `DeepCopyObject()` methods appear in `zz_generated.deepcopy.go`

### 4. **Scheme Registration**
- `SchemeBuilder` in `pkg/runtime/scheme_builder.go` provides the registration pattern
- `Scheme` in `pkg/runtime/scheme.go` manages the type registry
- `staging/src/k8s.io/api/core/v1/register.go` registers all core/v1 types

### 5. **Core/v1 Types Implementing runtime.Object**
The answer identifies **43+ concrete types** including:
- Core workload types (Pod, Node, Service, Namespace)
- Storage types (PersistentVolume, PersistentVolumeClaim, Secret, ConfigMap)
- Control plane types (Event, Binding, ComponentStatus)
- Options/proxy types (PodAttachOptions, PodLogOptions, etc.)
- Plus corresponding List types for all resources

Core Runtime.Object Definition\\nThe `runtime.Object` interface is defined in `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime/interfaces.go` (lines 337-340) and requires two methods:\\n- `GetObjectKind() schema.ObjectKind` - provides access to the object's type metadata\\n- `DeepCopyObject() Object` - creates a deep copy of the object\\n\\nThis interface is the foundation for all Kubernetes API objects that can be serialized, stored, and manipulated by the API machinery.\\n\\n### 2. Type and Meta Implementation\\nThe `TypeMeta` and `ObjectMeta` types from `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1/meta.go` provide the base fields that enable runtime.Object implementation. Code Generation for DeepCopyObject\\nThe deepcopy-gen code generator (controlled by the `// +k8s:deepcopy-gen:interfaces=k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime.Object` directive in type definitions) automatically generates `DeepCopyObject()` methods for all core/v1 types. These implementations are in `zz_generated.deepcopy.go` and delegate to the generated `DeepCopy()` method.\\n\\nCore/v1 types implementing runtime.Object include:\\n- **Pod** - Container execution unit\\n- **Node** - Cluster node resource\\n- **Service** - Network service abstraction\\n- **Namespace** - Resource grouping and isolation\\n- **Binding** - Pod-to-node binding\\n- **Event** - API event record\\n- **PersistentVolume** & **PersistentVolumeClaim** - Storage abstractions\\n- **Secret** & **ConfigMap** - Configuration storage\\n- **ServiceAccount** - Authentication identity\\n- **ReplicationController** - Workload replication (legacy)\\n- **PodTemplate** - Pod template definition\\n- **Endpoints** - Service endpoint address list\\n- **LimitRange** & **ResourceQuota** - Resource constraints\\n- **ComponentStatus** - Component health status\\n- **RangeAllocation** & **SerializedReference** - Internal types\\n- **Pod*Options** types (AttachOptions, LogOptions, ExecOptions, PortForwardOptions, ProxyOptions)\\n- **ServiceProxyOptions** & **NodeProxyOptions** - Proxy configuration\\n- Plus corresponding List types for all resources\\n\\n### 4. Scheme Registration Pattern\\nThe Kubernetes Scheme provides the type registry for runtime.Object implementations. The scheme is built using:\\n\\n1. **SchemeBuilder** (`pkg/runtime/scheme_builder.go`) - A builder pattern that collects registration functions\\n2. **Scheme** (`pkg/runtime/scheme.go`) - Manages mappings between Go types and Kubernetes GroupVersionKind metadata\\n3. **addKnownTypes function** (`staging/src/k8s.io/api/core/v1/register.go`) - Explicitly registers all core/v1 types with their GroupVersion\\n\\nThe registration in core/v1/register.go creates a SchemeBuilder with `runtime.NewSchemeBuilder(addKnownTypes)` and exposes it via `AddToScheme`, enabling each package to declaratively register its API types with any Scheme.\\n\\n### 5. Import Chain Summary\\nThe import chain flows as follows:\\n- `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime.Object` interface is the root abstraction\\n- Embedded in types via `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1.TypeMeta` and `.ObjectMeta`\\n- Code generators create `DeepCopyObject()` methods for marked types\\n- `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime.SchemeBuilder` provides registration infrastructure\\n- `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime.Scheme` manages the full type registry\\n- `staging/src/k8s.io/api/core/v1/register.go` registers concrete core/v1 types into the scheme\\n\\nThis design decouples API type definitions from the runtime machinery, allowing the same Object interface and Scheme infrastructure to work across all Kubernetes API groups and versions.\"\n}\n",

The scheme is built using:\\n\\n1. **SchemeBuilder** (`pkg/runtime/scheme_builder.go`) - A builder pattern that collects registration functions\\n2. **Scheme** (`pkg/runtime/scheme.go`) - Manages mappings between Go types and Kubernetes GroupVersionKind metadata\\n3. **addKnownTypes function** (`staging/src/k8s.io/api/core/v1/register.go`) - Explicitly registers all core/v1 types with their GroupVersion\\n\\nThe registration in core/v1/register.go creates a SchemeBuilder with `runtime.NewSchemeBuilder(addKnownTypes)` and exposes it via `AddToScheme`, enabling each package to declaratively register its API types with any Scheme.\\n\\n### 5.
